# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Produce answer.json** — Write ALL output to `/workspace/answer.json` with this structure:
   ```json
   {
     "analysis": {
       "summary": "Brief description of your approach",
       "files_examined": [{"path": "file.ext", "description": "..."}],
       "reasoning": "Detailed explanation or analysis"
     },
     "changes": [
       {"file": "path.ext", "description": "...", "diff": "unified diff"}
     ]
   }
   ```
   Omit `changes` if the task is analysis-only. Do NOT edit source files directly — produce diffs in `changes[]` instead.

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

# Kubernetes RBAC ClusterRole Privilege Escalation Paths

## Your Task

Audit kubernetes/kubernetes for RBAC privilege escalation paths. Find all Go source files that validate ClusterRole escalation rules — specifically, the files that enforce the 'escalation' verb restriction and prevent users from granting permissions they don't hold.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive audit of the Kubernetes RBAC privilege escalation prevention system. Here's what I found:

## Summary

I've identified **9 critical Go source files** that enforce RBAC escalation rules and prevent users from granting permissions they don't hold:

### Core Escalation Validation Files:

1. **pkg/registry/rbac/escalation_check.go** - Primary escalation control with:
   - `EscalationAllowed()` - Allows superusers (system:masters group)
   - `RoleEscalationAuthorized()` - Checks the "escalate" verb authorization
   - `BindingAuthorized()` - Verifies binding authorization

2. **pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go** - Permission validation with:
   - `ConfirmNoEscalation()` - Core function preventing privilege escalation
   - `DefaultRuleResolver` - Resolves user's current permissions

3. **Storage Layer** (4 files) - Enforces checks on Create/Update:
   - `pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrole/policybased/storage.go`
   - `pkg/registry/rbac/role/policybased/storage.go`
   - `pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrolebinding/policybased/storage.go`
   - `pkg/registry/rbac/rolebinding/policybased/storage.go`

### Key Control Points:

- **'escalate' verb**: The critical authorization gate that controls explicit privilege escalation
- **Coverage validation**: Uses `Covers()` from `staging/src/k8s.io/component-helpers/auth/rbac/validation/policy_comparator.go` to verify new permissions are within user's scope
- **GC field mutations**: `IsOnlyMutatingGCFields()` allows cleanup operations without escalation

The complete validation chain prevents users from creating roles, role bindings, or cluster role bindings with permissions they don't currently possess.

All findings have been written to `/workspace/answer.json`.

It:\\n   - Retrieves the user's current rules via the DefaultRuleResolver\\n   - Uses the staging/src/k8s.io/component-helpers/auth/rbac/validation/policy_comparator.go Covers() function to verify the new rules are covered by existing user permissions\\n   - Rejects the operation with a 'Forbidden' error if the user attempts to grant new capabilities\\n\\n5. **Storage Layer Enforcement**: Each RBAC resource storage layer applies these checks:\\n   - ClusterRole storage.go (lines 73-91): Checks EscalationAllowed or RoleEscalationAuthorized before allowing role creation with ConfirmNoEscalationInternal validation\\n   - Role storage.go (lines 67-77): Similar checks for namespaced roles\\n   - ClusterRoleBinding storage.go (lines 69-91): Checks EscalationAllowed, BindingAuthorized, and ConfirmNoEscalation before creating bindings\\n   - RoleBinding storage.go (lines 70-99): Similar checks for namespaced role bindings\\n\\n6. **GC-Only Mutations (IsOnlyMutatingGCFields)**: In pkg/registry/rbac/helpers.go, this function allows non-escalating users to update finalizers and owner references needed for garbage collection, preventing accidental denial of service during cleanup.\\n\\nThe complete escalation prevention chain flows from storage.Create/Update \u2192 EscalationAllowed/RoleEscalationAuthorized \u2192 ConfirmNoEscalation \u2192 Covers, ensuring that at each stage, users cannot grant permissions beyond their current scope.
